   <div class="mw-indicators">
   </div>
   <h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">
    Assyria
   </h1>
   <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
    <div id="siteSub">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div>
    <div id="contentSub">
    </div>
    <div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">
     Jump to:
     <a href="#mw-head">
      navigation
     </a>
     ,
     <a href="#p-search">
      search
     </a>
    </div>
    <div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en">
     <div class="hatnote">
      This article is about ancient Assyria.  For other uses, see
      <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Assyria_(disambiguation)" title="Assyria (disambiguation)">
       Assyria (disambiguation)
      </a>
      .
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote">
      "Assyrian Empire" redirects here. For the most powerful stage of the ancient Assyrian state, see
      <a href="/wiki/Neo-Assyrian_Empire" title="Neo-Assyrian Empire">
       Neo-Assyrian Empire
      </a>
      .
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ancient_Egypt_and_Mesopotamia_c._1450_BC.png">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1473" data-file-width="1200" height="270" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Ancient_Egypt_and_Mesopotamia_c._1450_BC.png/220px-Ancient_Egypt_and_Mesopotamia_c._1450_BC.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Ancient_Egypt_and_Mesopotamia_c._1450_BC.png/330px-Ancient_Egypt_and_Mesopotamia_c._1450_BC.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Ancient_Egypt_and_Mesopotamia_c._1450_BC.png/440px-Ancient_Egypt_and_Mesopotamia_c._1450_BC.png 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ancient_Egypt_and_Mesopotamia_c._1450_BC.png" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Overview map of the Ancient Near East in the 15th century BC (Middle Assyrian period), showing the core territory of Assyria with its two major cities
        <a href="/wiki/Assur" title="Assur">
         Assur
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Nineveh" title="Nineveh">
         Nineveh
        </a>
        wedged between
        <a href="/wiki/Babylonia" title="Babylonia">
         Babylonia
        </a>
        downstream (to the south-east) and the states of
        <a href="/wiki/Mitanni" title="Mitanni">
         Mitanni
        </a>
        and
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hittite_Empire" title="Hittite Empire">
         Hatti
        </a>
        upstream (to the north-west).
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      <b>
       Assyria
      </b>
      was a major
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mesopotamian" title="Mesopotamian">
       Mesopotamian
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/East_Semitic_languages" title="East Semitic languages">
       East Semitic
      </a>
      kingdom, and empire, of the
      <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Near_East" title="Ancient Near East">
       Ancient Near East
      </a>
      , existing as an independent state for a period of approximately six centuries from c. 1250 BC to 612 BC, spanning the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Early_Bronze_Age" title="Early Bronze Age">
       Early Bronze Age
      </a>
      through to the late
      <a href="/wiki/Iron_Age" title="Iron Age">
       Iron Age
      </a>
      . For a further thirteen centuries, from the end of the 7th century BC to the mid-7th century AD, it survived as a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Geo-political" title="Geo-political">
       geo-political
      </a>
      entity, for the most part ruled by foreign powers, although a number of small
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neo-Assyrian" title="Neo-Assyrian">
       Neo-Assyrian
      </a>
      states such as
      <a href="/wiki/Assur" title="Assur">
       Assur
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Adiabene" title="Adiabene">
       Adiabene
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Osroene" title="Osroene">
       Osroene
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Hatra" title="Hatra">
       Hatra
      </a>
      arose at different times between the 1st century BC and late 3rd century AD.
     </p>
     <p>
      Centered on the Upper
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tigris_river" title="Tigris river">
       Tigris river
      </a>
      , in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Northern_Mesopotamia" title="Northern Mesopotamia">
       northern Mesopotamia
      </a>
      (modern northern
      <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">
       Iraq
      </a>
      , northeastern
      <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">
       Syria
      </a>
      and southeastern
      <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">
       Turkey
      </a>
      ) the Assyrians came to rule powerful empires at several times.
     </p>
     <p>
      As a substantial part of the greater
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mesopotamian" title="Mesopotamian">
       Mesopotamian
      </a>
      "
      <a href="/wiki/Cradle_of_civilization" title="Cradle of civilization">
       cradle of civilization
      </a>
      " which included
      <a href="/wiki/Sumer" title="Sumer">
       Sumer
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Akkadian_Empire" title="Akkadian Empire">
       Akkad
      </a>
      and much later
      <a href="/wiki/Babylonia" title="Babylonia">
       Babylonia
      </a>
      , Assyria was at the height of technological, scientific and cultural achievements for its time. At its peak, the Assyrian empire stretched from
      <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">
       Cyprus
      </a>
      in the Mediterranean Sea to
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Persia" title="Persia">
       Persia
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">
       Iran
      </a>
      ), and from what is now
      <a href="/wiki/Armenia" title="Armenia">
       Armenia
      </a>
      to the
      <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Peninsula" title="Arabian Peninsula">
       Arabian Peninsula
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">
       Egypt
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Assyria is named for its original capital, the ancient city of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/A%C5%A1%C5%A1ur" title="Aur">
       Aur
      </a>
      (a.k.a.
      <a href="/wiki/Ashur" title="Ashur">
       Ashur
      </a>
      ) which dates to c. 2600 BC (located in what is now the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saladin_Province" title="Saladin Province">
       Saladin Province
      </a>
      of northern
      <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">
       Iraq
      </a>
      ), originally one of a number of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Akkadian" title="Akkadian">
       Akkadian
      </a>
      city states in Mesopotamia. In the 25th and 24th centuries BC, Assyrian kings were pastoral leaders, and from the late 24th century BC became subject to
      <a href="/wiki/Sargon_of_Akkad" title="Sargon of Akkad">
       Sargon of Akkad
      </a>
      , who united all the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Akkadian" title="Akkadian">
       Akkadian
      </a>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Semites" title="Semites">
       Semites
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Sumerian_language" title="Sumerian language">
       Sumerian
      </a>
      -speaking peoples of Mesopotamia under the
      <a href="/wiki/Akkadian_Empire" title="Akkadian Empire">
       Akkadian Empire
      </a>
      , which lasted from c. 2334 BC to 2154 BC. Following the fall of the Akkadian Empire c. 2154 BC,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-1">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        1
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and the short lived succeeding
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neo-Sumerian_Empire" title="Neo-Sumerian Empire">
       Neo-Sumerian Empire
      </a>
      which ruled southern Assyria but not the north, Assyria regained full independence.
     </p>
     <p>
      The history of Assyria proper is roughly divided into three periods, known as Old Assyrian, Middle Assyrian and Neo-Assyrian. These terms are in wide use in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Assyrology" title="Assyrology">
       Assyrology
      </a>
      and roughly correspond to the early to
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Middle_Bronze_Age" title="Middle Bronze Age">
       Middle Bronze Age
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Late_Bronze_Age" title="Late Bronze Age">
       Late Bronze Age
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Early_Iron_Age" title="Early Iron Age">
       Early Iron Age
      </a>
      , respectively. In the Old Assyrian period, Assyria established colonies in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asia_Minor" title="Asia Minor">
       Asia Minor
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Levant" title="The Levant">
       the Levant
      </a>
      and, under king
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ilushuma" title="Ilushuma">
       Ilushuma
      </a>
      , it asserted itself over southern Mesopotamia. From the mid 18th century BC, Assyria came into conflict with the newly created state of
      <a href="/wiki/Babylonia" title="Babylonia">
       Babylonia
      </a>
      , which eventually eclipsed the far older Sumero-Akkadian states in the south, such as
      <a href="/wiki/Ur" title="Ur">
       Ur
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Isin" title="Isin">
       Isin
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Larsa" title="Larsa">
       Larsa
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Kish_(Sumer)" title="Kish (Sumer)">
       Kish
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Assyria experienced fluctuating fortunes in the Old Assyrian period. Assyria became a regionally powerful nation with the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Old_Assyrian_Empire" title="Old Assyrian Empire">
       Old Assyrian Empire
      </a>
      from the late 21st century to the mid 18th century BC. Following this, it found itself under short periods of Babylonian and
      <a href="/wiki/Mitanni" title="Mitanni">
       Mitanni
      </a>
      -
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurrian" title="Hurrian">
       Hurrian
      </a>
      rule in the 18th and 15th centuries BC respectively, and another period of great power occurred with the rise of the
      <a href="/wiki/Middle_Assyrian_Empire" title="Middle Assyrian Empire">
       Middle Assyrian Empire
      </a>
      (from 1365 BC to 1056 BC), which included the reigns of great kings, such as
      <a href="/wiki/Ashur-uballit_I" title="Ashur-uballit I">
       Ashur-uballit I
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Arik-den-ili" title="Arik-den-ili">
       Arik-den-ili
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Tukulti-Ninurta_I" title="Tukulti-Ninurta I">
       Tukulti-Ninurta I
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Tiglath-Pileser_I" title="Tiglath-Pileser I">
       Tiglath-Pileser I
      </a>
      . During this period, Assyria overthrew the
      <a href="/wiki/Mitanni" title="Mitanni">
       Mitanni
      </a>
      -Empire and eclipsed the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hittite_Empire" title="Hittite Empire">
       Hittite Empire
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Egyptian_Empire" title="Egyptian Empire">
       Egyptian Empire
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Babylonia" title="Babylonia">
       Babylonia
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Elam" title="Elam">
       Elam
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Phrygia" title="Phrygia">
       Phrygia
      </a>
      in the
      <a href="/wiki/Near_East" title="Near East">
       Near East
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Beginning with the campaigns of
      <a href="/wiki/Adad-nirari_II" title="Adad-nirari II">
       Adad-nirari II
      </a>
      from 911 BC,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Georges_Roux.2C_Ancient_Iraq_2-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Georges_Roux.2C_Ancient_Iraq-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      it again became a great power over the next three centuries, overthrowing the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Twenty-fifth_dynasty_of_Egypt" title="Twenty-fifth dynasty of Egypt">
       Twenty-fifth dynasty of Egypt
      </a>
      and conquering
      <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">
       Egypt
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Georges_Roux.2C_Ancient_Iraq_2-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Georges_Roux.2C_Ancient_Iraq-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Babylonia,
      <a href="/wiki/Elam" title="Elam">
       Elam
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Urartu" title="Urartu">
       Urartu
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Armenians" title="Armenians">
       Armenia
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Media_(region)" title="Media (region)">
       Media
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Persia" title="Persia">
       Persia
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Mannaeans" title="Mannaeans">
       Mannea
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gutium" title="Gutium">
       Gutium
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Phoenicia" title="Phoenicia">
       Phoenicia
      </a>
      /
      <a href="/wiki/Canaan" title="Canaan">
       Canaan
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aramea" title="Aramea">
       Aramea
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">
       Syria
      </a>
      ),
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabia" title="Arabia">
       Arabia
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Israel_(Samaria)" title="Kingdom of Israel (Samaria)">
       Israel
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Judah" title="Kingdom of Judah">
       Judah
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Edom" title="Edom">
       Edom
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Moab" title="Moab">
       Moab
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Ammon" title="Ammon">
       Ammon
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Samarra" title="Samarra">
       Samarra
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Cilicia" title="Cilicia">
       Cilicia
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">
       Cyprus
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Chaldea" title="Chaldea">
       Chaldea
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nabatea" title="Nabatea">
       Nabatea
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commagene" title="Commagene">
       Commagene
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Dilmun" title="Dilmun">
       Dilmun
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">
       Libya
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Hurrians" title="Hurrians">
       Hurrians
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Sutu,_Iran" title="Sutu, Iran">
       Sutu
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neo-Hittites" title="Neo-Hittites">
       Neo-Hittites
      </a>
      , driving the
      <a href="/wiki/People_of_Ethiopia" title="People of Ethiopia">
       Ethiopians
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kushites" title="Kushites">
       Kushites
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Nubians" title="Nubians">
       Nubians
      </a>
      from Egypt,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Georges_Roux.2C_Ancient_Iraq_2-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-Georges_Roux.2C_Ancient_Iraq-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      subjugating the
      <a href="/wiki/Cimmerians" title="Cimmerians">
       Cimmerians
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Scythians" title="Scythians">
       Scythians
      </a>
      and exacting tribute from
      <a href="/wiki/Phrygia" title="Phrygia">
       Phrygia
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Majan_(civilization)" title="Majan (civilization)">
       Magan
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Land_of_Punt" title="Land of Punt">
       Punt
      </a>
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify">
         <span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (April 2014)">
          clarification needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      among others.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Georges_Roux.2C_Ancient_Iraq_2-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-Georges_Roux.2C_Ancient_Iraq-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      After its fall (between 612 BC and 605 BC), Assyria remained a province and geo-political entity under the Babylonian, Median,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Achaemenid" title="Achaemenid">
       Achaemenid
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seleucid" title="Seleucid">
       Seleucid
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Parthian_Empire" title="Parthian Empire">
       Parthian
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">
       Roman
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sassanid" title="Sassanid">
       Sassanid
      </a>
      empires until the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arab" title="Arab">
       Arab
      </a>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Islamic" title="Islamic">
       Islamic
      </a>
      invasion and conquest of Mesopotamia in the mid-7th century AD, when it was finally dissolved, after which the remnants of the
      <a href="/wiki/Assyrian_people" title="Assyrian people">
       Assyrian people
      </a>
      (by now almost exclusively
      <a href="/wiki/East_Syrian_Rite" title="East Syrian Rite">
       Eastern Rite
      </a>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Assyrian_Christians" title="Assyrian Christians">
       Assyrian Christians
      </a>
      ) gradually became an ethnic, linguistic, cultural and religious minority in the traditional
      <a href="/wiki/Assyrian_homeland" title="Assyrian homeland">
       Assyrian homelands
      </a>
      , surviving there to this day. (see
      <a href="/wiki/Assyrian_continuity" title="Assyrian continuity">
       Assyrian continuity
      </a>
      ).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Parpola.2C_Simo_2004_3-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Parpola.2C_Simo_2004-3">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        3
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
     </p>
