      <a href="/wiki/Nimrod" title="Nimrod">
       Nimrod
      </a>
      in the Old Testament.
     </p>
     <p>
      However, Tukulti-Ninurta's sons rebelled and besieged the ageing king in his capital. He was murdered and then succeeded by
      <a href="/wiki/Ashur-nadin-apli" title="Ashur-nadin-apli">
       Ashur-nadin-apli
      </a>
      (12061203 BC) who left the running of his empire to Assyrian regional governors such as
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Adad-b%C4%93l-gabbe&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Adad-bl-gabbe (page does not exist)">
       Adad-bl-gabbe
      </a>
      . Another unstable period for Assyria followed, it was riven by periods of internal strife and the new king only made token and unsuccessful attempts to recapture Babylon, whose Kassite kings had taken advantage of the upheavals in Assyria and freed themselves from Assyrian rule. However, Assyria itself was not threatened by foreign powers during the reigns of
      <a href="/wiki/Ashur-nirari_III" title="Ashur-nirari III">
       Ashur-nirari III
      </a>
      (12021197 BC),
      <a href="/wiki/Enlil-kudurri-usur" title="Enlil-kudurri-usur">
       Enlil-kudurri-usur
      </a>
      (11961193 BC) and
      <a href="/wiki/Ninurta-apal-Ekur" title="Ninurta-apal-Ekur">
       Ninurta-apal-Ekur
      </a>
      (11921180 BC), although Ninurta-apal-Ekur usurped the throne from Enlil-kudurri-usur.
     </p>
     <p>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ashur-Dan_I" title="Ashur-Dan I">
       Ashur-Dan I
      </a>
      (11791133 BC) stabilised the internal unrest in Assyria during his unusually long reign, quelling instability. During the twilight years of the Kassite dynasty in Babylonia, he
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
       <a href="#cite_note-30">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        29
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      records that he seized northern Babylonia, including the cities of
      <a href="/wiki/Zaban" title="Zaban">
       Zaban
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Irriya&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Irriya (page does not exist)">
       Irriya
      </a>
      and
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ugar-sallu&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ugar-sallu (page does not exist)">
       Ugar-sallu
      </a>
      during the reigns of
      <a href="/wiki/Marduk-apla-iddina_I" title="Marduk-apla-iddina I">
       Marduk-apla-iddina I
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Zababa-shuma-iddin" title="Zababa-shuma-iddin">
       Zababa-shuma-iddin
      </a>
      , plundering them and "taking their vast booty to Assyria." However, the conquest of northern Babylonia brought Assyria into direct conflict with Elam which had taken the remainder of Babylonia. The powerful Elamites, under king
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shutruk-Nahhunte" title="Shutruk-Nahhunte">
       Shutruk-Nahhunte
      </a>
      , fresh from sacking Babylon, entered into a protracted war with Assyria, they briefly took the Assyrian city of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arrapkha" title="Arrapkha">
       Arrapkha
      </a>
      , which Ashur-Dan I then retook, eventually defeating the Elamites and forcing a treaty upon them in the process.
     </p>
     <p>
      Another very brief period of internal upheaval followed the death of Ashur-Dan I when his son and successor
      <a href="/wiki/Ninurta-tukulti-Ashur" title="Ninurta-tukulti-Ashur">
       Ninurta-tukulti-Ashur
      </a>
      (1133 BC) was deposed in his first year of rule by his own brother
      <a href="/wiki/Mutakkil-Nusku" title="Mutakkil-Nusku">
       Mutakkil-Nusku
      </a>
      and forced to flee to Babylonia.
      <a href="/wiki/Mutakkil-Nusku" title="Mutakkil-Nusku">
       Mutakkil-Nusku
      </a>
      himself died in the same year (1133 BC).
     </p>
     <p>
      A third brother,
      <a href="/wiki/Ashur-resh-ishi_I" title="Ashur-resh-ishi I">
       Ashur-resh-ishi I
      </a>
      (11331116 BC) took the throne. This was to lead to a renewed period of Assyrian expansion and empire. As the Hittite empire collapsed from the onslaught of the Indo-European
      <a href="/wiki/Phrygians" title="Phrygians">
       Phrygians
      </a>
      (called
      <a href="/wiki/Mushki" title="Mushki">
       Mushki
      </a>
      in Assyrian annals), Babylon and Assyria began to vie for Aramaean regions (in modern Syria), formerly under firm Hittite control. When their forces encountered one another in this region, the Assyrian king
      <a href="/wiki/Ashur-resh-ishi_I" title="Ashur-resh-ishi I">
       Ashur-resh-ishi I
      </a>
      met and defeated
      <a href="/wiki/Nebuchadnezzar_I" title="Nebuchadnezzar I">
       Nebuchadnezzar I
      </a>
      of Babylon on a number of occasions. Assyria then invaded and annexed Hittite-controlled lands in Asia Minor, Aram (Syria), and Gutians and Kassite regions in the Zagros, marking an upsurge in imperian expansion.
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Tiglath-Pileser_I" title="Tiglath-Pileser I">
       Tiglath-Pileser I
      </a>
      (11151077 BC), vies with
      <a href="/wiki/Shamshi-Adad_I" title="Shamshi-Adad I">
       Shamshi-Adad I
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Ashur-uballit_I" title="Ashur-uballit I">
       Ashur-uballit I
      </a>
      among historians as being regarded as the founder of the first Assyrian empire. The son of Ashur-resh-ishi I, he ascended to the throne upon his father's death, and became one of the greatest of Assyrian conquerors during his 38-year reign.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hugh_Chrisholm_1911.2C_p._968_31-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Hugh_Chrisholm_1911.2C_p._968-31">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        30
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      His first campaign in 1112 BC was against the Phrygians who had attempted to occupy certain Assyrian districts in the Upper Euphrates region of Asia Minor; after defeating and driving out the Phrygians he then overran the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Luwian" title="Luwian">
       Luwian
      </a>
      kingdoms of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commagene" title="Commagene">
       Commagene
      </a>
      , Cilicia and Cappadocia in western Asia Minor, and drove the Neo-Hittites from the Assyrian province of Subartu, northeast of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Malatia" title="Malatia">
       Malatia
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      In a subsequent campaign, the Assyrian forces penetrated Urartu, into the mountains south of
      <a href="/wiki/Lake_Van" title="Lake Van">
       Lake Van
      </a>
      and then turned westward to receive the submission of Malatia. In his fifth year, Tiglath-Pileser again attacked Commagene, Cilicia and Cappadocia, and placed a record of his victories engraved on copper plates in a fortress he built to secure his Anatolian conquests.
     </p>
     <p>
      The Aramaeans of northern and central Syria were the next targets of the Assyrian king, who made his way as far as the sources of the Tigris.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hugh_Chrisholm_1911.2C_p._968_31-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Hugh_Chrisholm_1911.2C_p._968-31">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        30
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The control of the high road to the Mediterranean was secured by the possession of the Hittite town of
      <a href="/wiki/Pitru" title="Pitru">
       Pitru
      </a>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
       <a href="#cite_note-32">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        31
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      at the junction between the Euphrates and
      <a href="/wiki/Sajur" title="Sajur">
       Sajur
      </a>
      ; thence he proceeded to conquer the Canaanite/Phoenician city-states of
      <a href="/wiki/Byblos" title="Byblos">
       Byblos
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Tyre,_Lebanon" title="Tyre, Lebanon">
       Tyre
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Sidon" title="Sidon">
       Sidon
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Simyra" title="Simyra">
       Simyra
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Berytus" title="Berytus">
       Berytus
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Beirut" title="Beirut">
       Beirut
      </a>
      ),
      <a href="/wiki/Aradus" title="Aradus">
       Aradus
      </a>
      and finally
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arvad" title="Arvad">
       Arvad
      </a>
      where he embarked onto a ship to sail the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mediterranean" title="Mediterranean">
       Mediterranean
      </a>
      , on which he killed a
      <i>
       nahiru
      </i>
      or "sea-horse" (which
      <a href="/wiki/A._Leo_Oppenheim" title="A. Leo Oppenheim">
       A. Leo Oppenheim
      </a>
      translates as a
      <a href="/wiki/Narwhal" title="Narwhal">
       narwhal
      </a>
      ) in the sea.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hugh_Chrisholm_1911.2C_p._968_31-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-Hugh_Chrisholm_1911.2C_p._968-31">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        30
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He was passionately fond of hunting and was also a great builder. The general view is that the restoration of the temple of the gods
      <a href="/wiki/Ashur_(god)" title="Ashur (god)">
       Ashur
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Hadad" title="Hadad">
       Hadad
      </a>
      at the Assyrian capital of Assur (Ashur) was one of his initiatives.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hugh_Chrisholm_1911.2C_p._968_31-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-Hugh_Chrisholm_1911.2C_p._968-31">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        30
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He also invaded and defeated Babylon twice, assuming the old title "King of Sumer and Akkad", forcing tribute from Babylon, although he did not actually depose the actual king in Babylonia, where the old
      <i>
       Kassite Dynasty
      </i>
      had now succumbed to an Elamite one.
     </p>
     <p>
      He was succeeded by
      <a href="/wiki/Asharid-apal-Ekur" title="Asharid-apal-Ekur">
       Asharid-apal-Ekur
      </a>
      (10761074 BC) who reigned for just two years. His reign marked the elevation of the office of
      <i>
       ummnu
      </i>
      (royal scribe) in importance.
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Ashur-bel-kala" title="Ashur-bel-kala">
       Ashur-bel-kala
      </a>
      (10731056 BC) kept the vast empire together, campaigning successfully against Urartu and Phrygia to the north and the Arameans to the west. He maintained friendly relations with
      <a href="/wiki/Marduk-shapik-zeri" title="Marduk-shapik-zeri">
       Marduk-shapik-zeri
      </a>
      of Babylon, however upon the death of that king, he invaded Babylonia and deposed the new ruler
      <a href="/wiki/Kada%C5%A1man-Buria%C5%A1" title="Kadaman-Buria">
       Kadaman-Buria
      </a>
      , appointing
      <a href="/wiki/Adad-apla-iddina" title="Adad-apla-iddina">
       Adad-apla-iddina
      </a>
      as his vassal in Babylon. He built some of the earliest examples of both
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zoological_Gardens" title="Zoological Gardens">
       Zoological Gardens
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Botanical_Gardens" title="Botanical Gardens">
       Botanical Gardens
      </a>
      in Ashur, collecting all manner of animals and plants from his empire, and receiving a collection of exotic animals as tributes from Egypt.
     </p>
     <p>
      He was also a great hunter, describing his exploits "at the city of
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Araziqu&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Araziqu (page does not exist)">
       Araziqu
      </a>
      which is before the land of Hatti and at the foot of
      <a href="/wiki/Mount_Lebanon" title="Mount Lebanon">
       Mount Lebanon
      </a>
      ." These locations show that well into his reign Assyria still controlled a vast empire.
     </p>
     <p>
      Late in his reign, the Middle Assyrian Empire erupted into civil war, when a rebellion was orchestrated by
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Tukulti-Mer&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Tukulti-Mer (page does not exist)">
       Tukulti-Mer
      </a>
      , a pretender to the throne of Assyria. Ashur-bel-kala eventually crushed Tukulti-Mer and his allies, however the civil war in Assyria had allowed hordes of Arameans to take advantage of the situation, and press in on Assyrian controlled territory from the west. Ashur-bel-kala counterattacked them, and conquered as far as Carchemish and the source of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Khabur_river" title="Khabur river">
       Khabur river
      </a>
      , but by the end of his reign many of the areas of Syria and Phoenicia-Canaan to the west of these regions as far as the Mediterranean, previously under firm Assyrian control, were eventually lost to the Assyrian Empire.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Assyria_during_the_Bronze_Age_Collapse.2C_1055.E2.80.93936_BC">
       Assyria during the Bronze Age Collapse, 1055936 BC
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Assyria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Assyria during the Bronze Age Collapse, 1055936 BC">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bronze_Age_Collapse" title="Bronze Age Collapse">
       Bronze Age Collapse
      </a>
      from 1200 BC to 900 BC was a
      <a href="/wiki/Dark_Ages_(historiography)" title="Dark Ages (historiography)">
       dark age
      </a>
      for the entire
      <a href="/wiki/Near_East" title="Near East">
       Near East
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">
       North Africa
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asia_Minor" title="Asia Minor">
       Asia Minor
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Caucasus" title="Caucasus">
       Caucasus
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mediterranean" title="Mediterranean">
       Mediterranean
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Balkan" title="Balkan">
       Balkan
      </a>
      regions, with great upheavals and mass movements of people.
     </p>
     <p>
      Assyria and its empire were not unduly affected by these tumultuous events for some 150 years, perhaps the only ancient power that was not. However, upon the death of
      <a href="/wiki/Ashur-bel-kala" title="Ashur-bel-kala">
       Ashur-bel-kala
      </a>
      in 1056 BC, Assyria went into a
      <i>
       comparative
      </i>
      decline for the next 100 or so years. The empire shrank significantly, and by 1020 BC Assyria appears to have controlled only areas close to Assyria itself, essential to keeping trade routes open in eastern Aramea, south eastern Asia Minor central Mesopotamia and north western Iran.
     </p>
     <p>
      New
      <a href="/wiki/West_Semitic_languages" title="West Semitic languages">
       West Semitic
      </a>
      peoples such as the Arameans,
      <a href="/wiki/Chaldea" title="Chaldea">
       Chaldeans
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Suteans" title="Suteans">
       Suteans
      </a>
      moved into areas to the west and south of Assyria, including overrunning much of Babylonia to the south, Indo-European speaking
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iranic" title="Iranic">
       Iranic
      </a>
      peoples such as the
      <a href="/wiki/Medes" title="Medes">
       Medes
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Persian_people" title="Persian people">
       Persians
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parthians" title="Parthians">
       Parthians
      </a>
      moved into the lands to the east of Assyria, displacing the native Gutians and pressuring Elam and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mannea" title="Mannea">
       Mannea
      </a>
      (which were all ancient non Indo-European civilisations of Iran), and to the north the Phrygians overran the Hittites, a new Hurrian state named Urartu arose in the Caucasus, and Cimmerians,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colchians" title="Colchians">
       Colchians
      </a>
      (Georgians) and Scythians around the Black Sea and Caucasus. Egypt was divided and in disarray, and Israelites were battling with other fellow Semitic Canaanite peoples such as the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amalekites" title="Amalekites">
       Amalekites
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moabites" title="Moabites">
       Moabites
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Edomites" title="Edomites">
       Edomites
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ammonites" title="Ammonites">
       Ammonites
      </a>
      and the non-Semitic
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peleset" title="Peleset">
       Peleset
      </a>
      /
      <a href="/wiki/Philistines" title="Philistines">
       Philistines
      </a>
      (who have been conjectured to be one of the so-called
      <a href="/wiki/Sea_Peoples" title="Sea Peoples">
       Sea Peoples
      </a>
      )
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AK2013_33-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-AK2013-33">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        32
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Drews48_34-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Drews48-34">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        33
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      for the control of southern Canaan.
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Assyrian_horsemen_arabs.png">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="432" data-file-width="988" height="96" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Assyrian_horsemen_arabs.png/220px-Assyrian_horsemen_arabs.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Assyrian_horsemen_arabs.png/330px-Assyrian_horsemen_arabs.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Assyrian_horsemen_arabs.png/440px-Assyrian_horsemen_arabs.png 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Assyrian_horsemen_arabs.png" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Assyrian horsemen pursue defeated Arabs.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Despite the apparent weakness of Assyria in comparison to its former might, at heart it in fact remained a solid, well defended nation whose warriors were the best in the world.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
       <a href="#cite_note-35">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        34
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Assyria, with its stable monarchy, powerful army and secure borders was in a stronger position during this time than potential rivals such as Egypt, Babylonia, Elam, Phrygia, Urartu, Persia and Media
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
       <a href="#cite_note-36">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        35
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Kings such as
      <a href="/wiki/Ashur-bel-kala" title="Ashur-bel-kala">
       Ashur-bel-kala
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Eriba-Adad_II" title="Eriba-Adad II">
       Eriba-Adad II
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Ashur-rabi_II" title="Ashur-rabi II">
       Ashur-rabi II
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Ashurnasirpal_I" title="Ashurnasirpal I">
       Ashurnasirpal I
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Tiglath-Pileser_II" title="Tiglath-Pileser II">
       Tiglath-Pileser II
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ashur-Dan_II" title="Ashur-Dan II">
       Ashur-Dan II
      </a>
      successfully defended Assyria's borders and upheld stability during this tumultuous time.
     </p>
     <p>
      Assyrian kings during this period appear to have adopted a policy of maintaining and defending a compact, secure nation and satellite colonies immediately surrounding it, and interspersed this with sporadic punitive raids and invasions of neighbouring territories when the need arose.
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Eriba-Adad_II" title="Eriba-Adad II">
       Eriba-Adad II
      </a>
      ruled for only two years, and in that time continued to campaign against the Arameans and neo-Hittites before he was deposed by his elderly uncle
      <a href="/wiki/Shamshi-Adad_IV" title="Shamshi-Adad IV">
       Shamshi-Adad IV
      </a>
      (10531050 BC) who appears to have had an uneventful reign.
      <a href="/wiki/Ashurnasirpal_I" title="Ashurnasirpal I">
       Ashurnasirpal I
      </a>
      (10491031 BC) succeeded him, and during his reign he continued to campaign endlessly against the Arameans to the west. Assyria was also afflicted by famine during this period.
      <a href="/wiki/Shalmaneser_II" title="Shalmaneser II">
       Shalmaneser II
      </a>
      (10301019 BC) appears to have lost territory in the Levant to the Arameans, who also appear to have also occupied
      <a href="/wiki/Nairi" title="Nairi">
       Nairi
      </a>
      in southeast Asia Minor, hitherto an Assyrian colony.
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Ashur-nirari_IV" title="Ashur-nirari IV">
       Ashur-nirari IV
      </a>
      took the throne in 1018 BC, and captured the Babylonian city of
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Atlila&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Atlila (page does not exist)">
       Atlila
      </a>
      from
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Simbar-Shipak&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Simbar-Shipak (page does not exist)">
       Simbar-Shipak
      </a>
      and continued Assyrian campaigns against the Arameans. He was eventually deposed by his uncle
      <a href="/wiki/Ashur-rabi_II" title="Ashur-rabi II">
       Ashur-rabi II
      </a>
      in 1013 BC.
     </p>
     <p>
      During the reign of
      <a href="/wiki/Ashur-rabi_II" title="Ashur-rabi II">
       Ashur-rabi II
      </a>
      (1013972 BC) Aramaean tribes took the cities of
      <a href="/wiki/Pitru" title="Pitru">
       Pitru
      </a>
      and
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Mutkinu&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Mutkinu (page does not exist)">
       Mutkinu
      </a>
      (which had been taken and colonized by Tiglath Pileser I.) This event showed how far Assyria could assert itself militarily when the need arose. The Assyrian king attacked the Arameans, forced his way to the far off Mediterranean and constructed a
      <a href="/wiki/Stele" title="Stele">
       stele
      </a>
      in the area of
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Mount_Atalur&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Mount Atalur (page does not exist)">
       Mount Atalur
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
       <a href="#cite_note-37">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        36
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Ashur-resh-ishi_II" title="Ashur-resh-ishi II">
       Ashur-resh-ishi II
      </a>
      (971968 BC) in all likelihood a fairly elderly man due to the length of his father's reign, had a largely uneventful period of rule, concerning himself with defending Assyria's borders and conducting various rebuilding projects within Assyria.
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Tiglath-Pileser_II" title="Tiglath-Pileser II">
       Tiglath-Pileser II
      </a>
      (967936 BC) succeeded him, and reigned for 28 years. He maintained the policies of his recent predecessors, but appears to have had an uneventful reign.
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Neo-Assyrian_Empire.2C_911.E2.80.93612_BC">
       Neo-Assyrian Empire, 911612 BC
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Assyria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Neo-Assyrian Empire, 911612 BC">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Assyria.png">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1363" data-file-width="1983" height="206" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Map_of_Assyria.png/300px-Map_of_Assyria.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Map_of_Assyria.png/450px-Map_of_Assyria.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Map_of_Assyria.png/600px-Map_of_Assyria.png 2x" width="300"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Assyria.png" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Map of the Neo-Assyrian Empire and its expansions.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles:
      <a href="/wiki/Neo-Assyrian_Empire" title="Neo-Assyrian Empire">
       Neo-Assyrian Empire
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Military_history_of_the_Neo-Assyrian_Empire" title="Military history of the Neo-Assyrian Empire">
       Military history of the Neo-Assyrian Empire
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ashur-Dan_II" title="Ashur-Dan II">
       Ashur-Dan II
      </a>
      (935912 BC) oversaw a marked economic and organisational upturn in the fortunes of Assyria, laying the platform for it to once again forge an empire. He is recorded as having made successful punitive raids outside the borders of Assyria to clear
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aramaeans" title="Aramaeans">
       Aramean
      </a>
      and other tribal peoples from the regions surrounding Assyria in all directions. He concentrated on rebuilding Assyria within its natural borders, from
      <a href="/wiki/Tur_Abdin" title="Tur Abdin">
       Tur Abdin
      </a>
      to
      <a href="/wiki/Arrapha" title="Arrapha">
       Arrapha
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Kirkuk" title="Kirkuk">
       Kirkuk
      </a>
      ), he built government offices in all provinces, and created a major economic boost by providing ploughs throughout the land, which yielded record grain production.
     </p>
     <p>
      The Neo-Assyrian Empire is usually considered to have begun with the accession of
      <a href="/wiki/Adad-nirari_II" title="Adad-nirari II">
       Adad-nirari II
      </a>
      , in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/911_BC" title="911 BC">
       911 BC
      </a>
      , lasting until the fall of Nineveh at the hands of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Babylonians" title="Babylonians">
       Babylonians, Chaldeans
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Medes" title="Medes">
       Medes/Persians
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Scythians" title="Scythians">
       Scythians
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Cimmerians" title="Cimmerians">
       Cimmerians
      </a>
      in 612 BC.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
       <a href="#cite_note-38">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        37
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Expansion.2C_911.E2.80.93627_BC">
       Expansion, 911627 BC
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Assyria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Expansion, 911627 BC">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      When the ancient Dark Ages (which for Assyria lasted from 1050 to 936 BC) finally lifted, the world had changed dramatically. Ancient kingdoms such as Assyria, Babylonia, Elam and Egypt still endured, the Hittites did also, in the form of smaller Neo-Hittite states. A number of new states had arisen during the tumultuous time between 1200 and 936 BC, such as; Persia, Media, Parthia, Mannea, Israel, Urartu, Phrygia, Lydia, the Aramean and Phoenician states of the Levant, Doric Greece, Putria (Libya), Colchia, Tabal, Nubia/Kush. In addition, other nations and peoples; such as Chaldea, Judah, Scythia, Cimmeria, Samaria, Ethiopia, Nabatea, Armenia and the Arabs were to emerge in the following centuries.
     </p>
     <p>
      However, it was the ancient state of Assyria which would once more rise to prominence, and Assyria was to meet and defeat these new peoples, together with old foes, over the coming three centuries.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Georges_Roux.2C_Ancient_Iraq_2-7">
       <a href="#cite_note-Georges_Roux.2C_Ancient_Iraq-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Beginning with the campaigns of
      <a href="/wiki/Adad-nirari_II" title="Adad-nirari II">
       Adad-nirari II
      </a>
      (911-892 BC), Assyria once more became a great power, growing to be the greatest empire the world had yet seen. The new king firmly subjugated the areas that were previously only under nominal Assyrian vassalage, conquering and deporting troublesome
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aramaeans" title="Aramaeans">
       Aramean
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neo-Hittite" title="Neo-Hittite">
       Neo-Hittite
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurrian" title="Hurrian">
       Hurrian
      </a>
      populations in the north to far-off places. Adad-nirari II then twice attacked and defeated
      <a href="/wiki/Shamash-mudammiq" title="Shamash-mudammiq">
       Shamash-mudammiq
      </a>
      of
      <a href="/wiki/Babylonia" title="Babylonia">
       Babylonia
      </a>
      , annexing a large area of land north of the
      <a href="/wiki/Diyala_River" title="Diyala River">
       Diyala River
      </a>
      and the towns of
      <a href="/wiki/H%C4%ABt" title="Ht">
       Ht
      </a>
      and
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Zanqu&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Zanqu (page does not exist)">
       Zanqu
      </a>
      in mid Mesopotamia. Later in his reign, he made further gains against King
      <a href="/wiki/Nabu-shuma-ukin_I" title="Nabu-shuma-ukin I">
       Nabu-shuma-ukin I
      </a>
      of
      <a href="/wiki/Babylonia" title="Babylonia">
       Babylonia
      </a>
      . He then conquered
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Kadmuh&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Kadmuh (page does not exist)">
       Kadmuh
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nisibin" title="Nisibin">
       Nisibin
      </a>
      from the
      <a href="/wiki/Arameans" title="Arameans">
       Arameans
      </a>
      , and secured the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Khabur" title="Khabur">
       Khabur
      </a>
      region.
     </p>
     <p>
      His successor,
      <a href="/wiki/Tukulti-Ninurta_II" title="Tukulti-Ninurta II">
       Tukulti-Ninurta II
      </a>
      (891884 BC) consolidated Assyria's gains and expanded into the
      <a href="/wiki/Zagros_Mountains" title="Zagros Mountains">
       Zagros Mountains
      </a>
      in modern
      <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">
       Iran
      </a>
      , subjugating the newly arrived
      <a href="/wiki/Persian_people" title="Persian people">
       Persians
      </a>
      , Parthians and
      <a href="/wiki/Medes" title="Medes">
       Medes
      </a>
      as well as pushing into central
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asia_Minor" title="Asia Minor">
       Asia Minor
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Assyrian_Attack_on_a_Town.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1049" data-file-width="1600" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Assyrian_Attack_on_a_Town.jpg/220px-Assyrian_Attack_on_a_Town.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Assyrian_Attack_on_a_Town.jpg/330px-Assyrian_Attack_on_a_Town.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Assyrian_Attack_on_a_Town.jpg/440px-Assyrian_Attack_on_a_Town.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Assyrian_Attack_on_a_Town.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Assyrian attack on a town with archers and a wheeled battering ram, 865860 BC
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Ashurnasirpal_II" title="Ashurnasirpal II">
       Ashurnasirpal II
      </a>
      (883859 BC) was a fierce and ruthless ruler who advanced without opposition through
      <a href="/wiki/Aram_(biblical_region)" title="Aram (biblical region)">
       Aram
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Canaan" title="Canaan">
       Canaan
      </a>
      (modern
      <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">
       Syria
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lebannon" title="Lebannon">
       Lebannon
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">
       Jordan
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">
       Israel
      </a>
      ) and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asia_Minor" title="Asia Minor">
       Asia Minor
      </a>
      as far as the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mediterranean" title="Mediterranean">
       Mediterranean
      </a>
      and conquered and exacted tribute from
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aramea" title="Aramea">
       Aramea
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Phrygia" title="Phrygia">
       Phrygia
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Phoenicia" title="Phoenicia">
       Phoenicia
      </a>
      among others. Ashurnasirpal II also repressed revolts among the
      <a href="/wiki/Medes" title="Medes">
       Medes
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Persia" title="Persia">
       Persians
      </a>
      in the Zagros Mountains, and moved his capital to the city of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kalhu" title="Kalhu">
       Kalhu
      </a>
      (
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Calah" title="Calah">
       Calah
      </a>
      /
      <a href="/wiki/Nimrud" title="Nimrud">
       Nimrud
      </a>
      ). The palaces, temples and other buildings raised by him bear witness to a considerable development of wealth, science, architecture and art. He also built a number of new heavily fortified towns, such as
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Imgur-Enlil" title="Imgur-Enlil">
       Imgur-Enlil
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Balawat" title="Balawat">
       Balawat
      </a>
      ),
      <a href="/wiki/Tushhan" title="Tushhan">
       Tushhan
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Kar-Ashurnasirpal&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Kar-Ashurnasirpal (page does not exist)">
       Kar-Ashurnasirpal
      </a>
      and
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Nibarti-Ashur&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Nibarti-Ashur (page does not exist)">
       Nibarti-Ashur
      </a>
      . Ashurnasirpal II also had a keen interest in
      <a href="/wiki/Botany" title="Botany">
       Botany
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Zoology" title="Zoology">
       Zoology
      </a>
      ; collecting all manner of plants, seeds and animals to be displayed in Assyria.
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Shalmaneser_III" title="Shalmaneser III">
       Shalmaneser III
      </a>
      (858823 BC) had his authority challenged by a large alliance of a dozen nations, some of which were vassals, including;
      <a href="/wiki/Babylonia" title="Babylonia">
       Babylonia
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">
       Egypt
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Elam" title="Elam">
       Elam
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Persia" title="Persia">
       Persia
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Israel_(Samaria)" title="Kingdom of Israel (Samaria)">
       Israel
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hamath" title="Hamath">
       Hamath
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Phoenicia" title="Phoenicia">
       Phoenicia
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Arabs" title="Arabs">
       Arabs
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Arameans" title="Arameans">
       Arameans
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Suteans" title="Suteans">
       Suteans
      </a>
      and neo
      <a href="/wiki/Hittites" title="Hittites">
       Hittites
      </a>
      among others, fighting them to a standstill at the
      <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Qarqar" title="Battle of Qarqar">
       Battle of Qarqar
      </a>
      . The failure of this alliance prevented pharaoh
      <a href="/wiki/Osorkon_II" title="Osorkon II">
       Osorkon II
      </a>
      from regaining an Egyptian foothold in the Near East.
     </p>
     <p>
      Subsequent to this, Shalmaneser III attacked and reduced
      <a href="/wiki/Babylonia" title="Babylonia">
       Babylonia
      </a>
      to vassalage, including subjugating the
      <a href="/wiki/Chaldea" title="Chaldea">
       Chaldean
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aramean" title="Aramean">
       Aramean
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sutean" title="Sutean">
       Sutean
      </a>
      tribes settled within it. He then defeated
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aramea" title="Aramea">
       Aramea
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Israel_(Samaria)" title="Kingdom of Israel (Samaria)">
       Israel
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Moab" title="Moab">
       Moab
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Edom" title="Edom">
       Edom
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Urartu" title="Urartu">
       Urartu
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Phoenicia" title="Phoenicia">
       Phoenicia
      </a>
      , the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neo-Hittite" title="Neo-Hittite">
       Neo-Hittite
      </a>
      states and the desert dwelling
      <a href="/wiki/Arabs" title="Arabs">
       Arabs
      </a>
      of the Arabian Peninsula, forcing all of these to pay tribute to Assyria.
     </p>
     <p>
      It is in Assyrian accounts of the 850's BC, recorded during the reign of
      <a href="/wiki/Shalmaneser_III" title="Shalmaneser III">
       Shalmaneser III
      </a>
      , that the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arab_people" title="Arab people">
       Arabs
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Chaldea" title="Chaldea">
       Chaldeans
      </a>
      first enter the pages of written history.
     </p>
     <p>
      His armies penetrated to
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Caucasus" title="The Caucasus">
       The Caucasus
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Lake_Van" title="Lake Van">
       Lake Van
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/Taurus_Mountains" title="Taurus Mountains">
       Taurus Mountains
      </a>
      ; the Hittites around Carchemish were compelled to pay tribute, and the kingdoms of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hamath" title="Hamath">
       Hamath
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aram_Damascus" title="Aram Damascus">
       Aram Damascus
      </a>
      were subdued. In 831 BC, he received the submission of the
      <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">
       Georgian
      </a>
      kingdom of
      <a href="/wiki/Tabal" title="Tabal">
       Tabal
      </a>
      . He consolidated Assyrian control over the regions conquered by his predecessors and, by the end of his 27-year reign, Assyria was master of Mesopotamia, The Levant, western Iran, Israel, Jordan and much of Asia Minor. Due to old age, in the last 6 years of his reign he passed command of his armies to the "Turtanu" (General)
      <a href="/wiki/Dayyan-Assur" title="Dayyan-Assur">
       Dayyan-Assur
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jehu-Obelisk-cropped.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="999" data-file-width="1557" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Jehu-Obelisk-cropped.jpg/220px-Jehu-Obelisk-cropped.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Jehu-Obelisk-cropped.jpg/330px-Jehu-Obelisk-cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Jehu-Obelisk-cropped.jpg/440px-Jehu-Obelisk-cropped.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jehu-Obelisk-cropped.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Jehu" title="Jehu">
         Jehu
        </a>
        , king of
        <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Israel_(Samaria)" title="Kingdom of Israel (Samaria)">
         Israel
        </a>
        , bows before Shalmaneser III of Assyria, 825 BC
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      However, his successor,
      <a href="/wiki/Shamshi-Adad_V" title="Shamshi-Adad V">
       Shamshi-Adad V
      </a>
      (822-811 BC) (also known as
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Shamshi-Ramman_II&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Shamshi-Ramman II (page does not exist)">
       Shamshi-Ramman II
      </a>
      ), inherited an empire beset by civil war in Assyria itself. The first years of his reign saw a serious struggle for the succession of the aged Shalmaneser III. The revolt, which had broken out by 826 BC, was led by Shamshi-Adad's brother
      <a href="/wiki/Assur-danin-pal" title="Assur-danin-pal">
       Assur-danin-pal
      </a>
      . The rebellious brother, according to Shamshi-Adad's own inscriptions, succeeded in bringing to his side 27 important cities, including
      <a href="/wiki/Nineveh" title="Nineveh">
       Nineveh
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Babylon" title="Babylon">
       Babylon
      </a>
      . The rebellion lasted until 820 BC, preventing Assyria expanding its empire further until it was quelled.
     </p>
     <p>
      Later in his reign, Shamshi-Adad V successfully campaigned against both
      <a href="/wiki/Babylonia" title="Babylonia">
       Babylonia
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Elam" title="Elam">
       Elam
      </a>
      , and forced a treaty in Assyria's favour on the Babylonian king
      <a href="/wiki/Marduk-zakir-shumi_I" title="Marduk-zakir-shumi I">
       Marduk-zakir-shumi I
      </a>
      . In
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/814_BCE" title="814 BCE">
       814 BCE
      </a>
      , he won the battle of
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Dur-Papsukkal&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Dur-Papsukkal (page does not exist)">
       Dur-Papsukkal
      </a>
      against the new Babylonian king
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Murduk-balassu-iqbi&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Murduk-balassu-iqbi (page does not exist)">
       Murduk-balassu-iqbi
      </a>
      , and went on to subjugate the immigrant tribes of
      <a href="/wiki/Chaldea" title="Chaldea">
       Chaldeans
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Arameans" title="Arameans">
       Arameans
      </a>
      , and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sutean" title="Sutean">
       Suteans
      </a>
      who had recently settled in parts of
      <a href="/wiki/Babylonia" title="Babylonia">
       Babylonia
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      He was succeeded by
      <a href="/wiki/Adad-nirari_III" title="Adad-nirari III">
       Adad-nirari III
      </a>
      (810782 BC), who was merely a boy. The Empire was thus ruled by his mother, the famed queen
      <a href="/wiki/Semiramis" title="Semiramis">
       Semiramis
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Shammuramat" title="Shammuramat">
       Shammuramat
      </a>
      ), until 806 BC.
      <a href="/wiki/Semiramis" title="Semiramis">
       Semiramis
      </a>
      held the empire together, and appears to have campaigned successfully in subjugating the
      <a href="/wiki/Persian_people" title="Persian people">
       Persians
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parthians" title="Parthians">
       Parthians
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Medes" title="Medes">
       Medes
      </a>
      during her regency, leading to the later
      <a href="/wiki/Iranian_peoples" title="Iranian peoples">
       Iranian
      </a>
      and also
      <a href="/wiki/Greeks" title="Greeks">
       Greek
      </a>
      myths and legends surrounding her.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
       <a href="#cite_note-39">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        38
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 806 BC,
      <a href="/wiki/Adad-nirari_III" title="Adad-nirari III">
       Adad-nirari III
      </a>
      took the reins of power from
      <a href="/wiki/Semiramis" title="Semiramis">
       Semiramis
      </a>
      . He invaded the
      <a href="/wiki/Levant" title="Levant">
       Levant
      </a>
      and subjugated the
      <a href="/wiki/Arameans" title="Arameans">
       Arameans
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Phoenicians" title="Phoenicians">
       Phoenicians
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Philistines" title="Philistines">
       Philistines
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Israelites" title="Israelites">
       Israelites
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neo-Hittites" title="Neo-Hittites">
       Neo-Hittites
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moabites" title="Moabites">
       Moabites
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Edomites" title="Edomites">
       Edomites
      </a>
      . He entered
      <a href="/wiki/Damascus" title="Damascus">
       Damascus
      </a>
      and forced tribute upon its
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aramaeans" title="Aramaeans">
       Aramean
      </a>
      king
      <a href="/wiki/Ben-Hadad_III" title="Ben-Hadad III">
       Ben-Hadad III
      </a>
      . He next turned eastward to
      <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">
       Iran
      </a>
      , and subjugated the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Persia" title="Persia">
       Persians
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Medes" title="Medes">
       Medes
      </a>
      and the pre Iranian
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manneans" title="Manneans">
       Manneans
      </a>
      , penetrating as far north east as the
      <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">
       Caspian Sea
      </a>
      . He then turned south, forcing
      <a href="/wiki/Babylonia" title="Babylonia">
       Babylonia
      </a>
      to pay tribute. His next targets were the migrant
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aramean" title="Aramean">
       Aramean
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chaldean_Dynasty" title="Chaldean Dynasty">
       Chaldean
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Sutu,_Iran" title="Sutu, Iran">
       Sutu
      </a>
      tribes, who had settled in the far south eastern corner of Mesopotamia, whom he conquered and reduced to vassalage. Then the
      <a href="/wiki/Arabs" title="Arabs">
       Arabs
      </a>
      in the deserts of the
      <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Peninsula" title="Arabian Peninsula">
       Arabian Peninsula
      </a>
      to the south of Mesopotamia were invaded, vanquished and forced to pay tribute also.
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Human_headed_winged_bull_profile.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1438" data-file-width="1500" height="211" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Human_headed_winged_bull_profile.jpg/220px-Human_headed_winged_bull_profile.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Human_headed_winged_bull_profile.jpg/330px-Human_headed_winged_bull_profile.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Human_headed_winged_bull_profile.jpg/440px-Human_headed_winged_bull_profile.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Human_headed_winged_bull_profile.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        A
        <a href="/wiki/Lamassu" title="Lamassu">
         lamassu
        </a>
        from the palace of Sargon II at
        <a href="/wiki/Dur-Sharrukin" title="Dur-Sharrukin">
         Dur-Sharrukin
        </a>
        .
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      It is from this general period that the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cilician" title="Cilician">
       Cilician
      </a>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indo-Anatolian" title="Indo-Anatolian">
       Indo-Anatolian
      </a>
      term
      <i>
       Surai
      </i>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">
       Syria
      </a>
      ) first appears in historical record in what is now called the
      <a href="/wiki/%C3%87inek%C3%B6y_inscription" title="ineky inscription">
       ineky inscription
      </a>
      , not in reference to the region of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aramea" title="Aramea">
       Aramea
      </a>
      now encompassing modern Syria in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Levant" title="The Levant">
       The Levant
      </a>
      , but specifically and only to Assyria itself.
     </p>
     <p>
      Adad-nirari III died prematurely in 782 BC, which led to a temporary period of stagnation within the empire. Assyria continued its military dominance, however
      <a href="/wiki/Shalmaneser_IV" title="Shalmaneser IV">
       Shalmaneser IV
      </a>
      (782 - 773 BC) himself seems to have wielded little personal authority, and a victory over
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Argishti_I" title="Argishti I">
       Argishti I
      </a>
      , king of
      <a href="/wiki/Urartu" title="Urartu">
       Urartu
      </a>
      at
      <a href="/wiki/Til_Barsip" title="Til Barsip">
       Til Barsip
      </a>
      is accredited to an Assyrian General (
      <a href="/wiki/Turtanu" title="Turtanu">
       Turtanu
      </a>
      ) named
      <a href="/wiki/Shamshi-ilu" title="Shamshi-ilu">
       Shamshi-ilu
      </a>
      , who does not even bother to mention his king. Shamshi-ilu also scored victories over the
      <a href="/wiki/Arameans" title="Arameans">
       Arameans
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Phrygians" title="Phrygians">
       Phrygians
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Persian_people" title="Persian people">
       Persians
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neo-Hittites" title="Neo-Hittites">
       Neo-Hittites
      </a>
      , and again, takes personal credit at the expense of his king.
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Ashur-dan_III" title="Ashur-dan III">
       Ashur-dan III
      </a>
      ascended the throne in 772 BC. He proved to be a largely ineffectual ruler who was beset by internal rebellions in the cities of
      <a href="/wiki/Ashur" title="Ashur">
       Ashur
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arrapkha" title="Arrapkha">
       Arrapkha
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guzana" title="Guzana">
       Guzana
      </a>
      ; and his personal authority was checked by powerful generals, such as Shamshi-ilu. He failed to make any further gains in Babylonia, Canaan and
      <a href="/wiki/Aram_(biblical_region)" title="Aram (biblical region)">
       Aram
      </a>
      . His reign was also marred by
      <a href="/wiki/Plague_(disease)" title="Plague (disease)">
       Plague
      </a>
      and an ominous
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Solar_Eclipse" title="Solar Eclipse">
       Solar Eclipse
      </a>
      and, as with his predecessor, military victories were credited to Shamshi-ilu.
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Ashur-nirari_V" title="Ashur-nirari V">
       Ashur-nirari V
      </a>
      became king in 754 BC, the early part of his reign seems to have been one of permanent internal revolution, and he apprears to have barely left his palace in
      <a href="/wiki/Nineveh" title="Nineveh">
       Nineveh
      </a>
      . However later in his reign he led a number of successful campaigns in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asia_Minor" title="Asia Minor">
       Asia Minor
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/Levant" title="Levant">
       Levant
      </a>
      . He was deposed by
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tiglath-pileser_III" title="Tiglath-pileser III">
       Tiglath-pileser III
      </a>
      in 745 BC bringing a resurgence to Assyrian expansion.
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Tiglath-Pileser_III" title="Tiglath-Pileser III">
       Tiglath-Pileser III
      </a>
      (745727 BC), a usurper whose original name was
      <i>
       Pulu
      </i>
      , initiated a renewed period of Assyrian expansion;
      <a href="/wiki/Urartu" title="Urartu">
       Urartu
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Persia" title="Persia">
       Persia
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Median_Empire" title="Median Empire">
       Media
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mannea" title="Mannea">
       Mannea
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Babylonia" title="Babylonia">
       Babylonia
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabia" title="Arabia">
       Arabia
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Phoenicia" title="Phoenicia">
       Phoenicia
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Israel_(Samaria)" title="Kingdom of Israel (Samaria)">
       Israel
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Judah" title="Kingdom of Judah">
       Judah
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Samaria" title="Samaria">
       Samaria
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nabatea" title="Nabatea">
       Nabatea
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Chaldea" title="Chaldea">
       Chaldea
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">
       Cyprus
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Moab" title="Moab">
       Moab
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Edom" title="Edom">
       Edom
      </a>
      and the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neo-Hittites" title="Neo-Hittites">
       Neo-Hittites
      </a>
      were subjugated, Tiglath-Pileser III was declared king in
      <a href="/wiki/Babylon" title="Babylon">
       Babylon
      </a>
      and the Assyrian empire was now stretched from the
      <a href="/wiki/Caucasus_Mountains" title="Caucasus Mountains">
       Caucasus Mountains
      </a>
      to
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabia" title="Arabia">
       Arabia
      </a>
      and from the
      <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">
       Caspian Sea
      </a>
      to
      <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">
       Cyprus
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Tiglath-Pileser III had reorganised the Assyrian army into the first professional fighting force in history, he also incorporated conquered peoples into the imperial army to serve as light infantry, thus expanding the size of the army. He greatly improved the civil administration of his empire, reducing the influence of hitherto powerful nobles, regional governors and viceroys, and deporting troublesome peoples to other parts of his vast empire, setting the template for all future ancient empires
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
       <a href="#cite_note-40">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        39
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Tiglath-Pileser III also introduced
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mesopotamian" title="Mesopotamian">
       Mesopotamian
      </a>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Aramaic" title="Eastern Aramaic">
       Eastern Aramaic
      </a>
      as the
      <i>
       Lingua Franca
      </i>
      of Assyria and its vast empire, whose Akkadian infused descendant dialects still survive among the modern
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Assyrian_Christian" title="Assyrian Christian">
       Assyrian Christian
      </a>
      people to this day.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
       <a href="#cite_note-41">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        40
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Shalmaneser_V" title="Shalmaneser V">
       Shalmaneser V
      </a>
      (726723 BC) consolidated Assyrian power during his short reign, and repressed
      <a href="/wiki/Egyptians" title="Egyptians">
       Egyptian
      </a>
      attempts to gain a foothold in the near east, defeating and driving out Pharaoh
      <a href="/wiki/Shoshenq_V" title="Shoshenq V">
       Shoshenq V
      </a>
      from the region. He is mentioned in Biblical sources as having conquered
      <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">
       Israel
      </a>
      and being responsible for deporting the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ten_Lost_Tribes_of_Israel" title="Ten Lost Tribes of Israel">
       Ten Lost Tribes of Israel
      </a>
      to Assyria. He and his successor also brought the
      <a href="/wiki/Samaritans" title="Samaritans">
       Samaritans
      </a>
      , people originating from Babylon, Cuthah, Ava, Sepharvaim and Hamath, and settled them in the towns of Samaria to replace the Israelites.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
       <a href="#cite_note-42">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        41
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Loewenjagd_-645-635_Niniveh.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4288" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Loewenjagd_-645-635_Niniveh.JPG/220px-Loewenjagd_-645-635_Niniveh.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Loewenjagd_-645-635_Niniveh.JPG/330px-Loewenjagd_-645-635_Niniveh.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Loewenjagd_-645-635_Niniveh.JPG/440px-Loewenjagd_-645-635_Niniveh.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Loewenjagd_-645-635_Niniveh.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Relief showing a
        <a href="/wiki/Lion_hunting" title="Lion hunting">
         lion hunt
        </a>
        , from the north palace of
        <a href="/wiki/Nineveh" title="Nineveh">
         Nineveh
        </a>
        , 645-635 BC
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Sargon_II" title="Sargon II">
       Sargon II
      </a>
      (722705 BC) maintained the empire, driving the
      <a href="/wiki/Cimmerians" title="Cimmerians">
       Cimmerians
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Scythians" title="Scythians">
       Scythians
      </a>
      from
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ancient_Iran" title="Ancient Iran">
       Ancient Iran
      </a>
      , where they had invaded and attacked the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Persia" title="Persia">
       Persians
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Medes" title="Medes">
       Medes
      </a>
      , who were vassals of Assyria.
      <a href="/wiki/Deioces" title="Deioces">
       Deioces
      </a>
      , king of the Medes and Persians was then forced to pay tribute after launching a failed rebellion against Assyria. When in 720 BCE a revolt occurred in
      <a href="/wiki/Canaan" title="Canaan">
       Canaan
      </a>
      against
      <a href="/wiki/Sargon_II" title="Sargon II">
       Sargon II
      </a>
      , king Hanno sought the help of Pharaoh
      <a href="/wiki/Osorkon_IV" title="Osorkon IV">
       Osorkon IV
      </a>
      of the 22nd Dynasty of
      <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">
       Egypt
      </a>
      . The Egyptian king sent a general named
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Raia_(general)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Raia (general) (page does not exist)">
       Raia
      </a>
      as well as troops in order to support the neighboring ally. However, the coalition was defeated in battle at
      <a href="/wiki/Rafah" title="Rafah">
       Raphia
      </a>
      : Raia fled back to Egypt, Raphia and
      <a href="/wiki/Gaza_City" title="Gaza City">
       Gaza
      </a>
      were looted and Hanno was
      <a href="/wiki/Death_by_burning" title="Death by burning">
       burnt alive
      </a>
      by the Assyrians.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kk_43-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-kk-43">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        42
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-G3412_44-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-G3412-44">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        43
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <br/>
      In 716 BCE Sargon II crossed the Sinai and amassed an army on Egypt's border. Osorkon IV personally met the Assyrian king at the "
      <a href="/wiki/Brook_of_Egypt" title="Brook of Egypt">
       Brook of Egypt
      </a>
      " (most likely
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/El-Arish" title="El-Arish">
       el-Arish
      </a>
      ) and was forced pay tribute to Sargon II to avoid being invaded.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kk_43-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-kk-43">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        42
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mannea" title="Mannea">
       Mannea
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Cilicia" title="Cilicia">
       Cilicia
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Cappadocia" title="Cappadocia">
       Cappadocia
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commagene" title="Commagene">
       Commagene
      </a>
      were conquered,
      <a href="/wiki/Urartu" title="Urartu">
       Urartu
      </a>
      was ravaged, and
      <a href="/wiki/Babylonia" title="Babylonia">
       Babylonia
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Chaldea" title="Chaldea">
       Chaldea
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Aram_(biblical_region)" title="Aram (biblical region)">
       Aram
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Phoenicia" title="Phoenicia">
       Phoenicia
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Israel_(Samaria)" title="Kingdom of Israel (Samaria)">
       Israel
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabia" title="Arabia">
       Arabia
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">
       Cyprus
      </a>
      and the famed
      <a href="/wiki/Midas" title="Midas">
       Midas
      </a>
      (king of
      <a href="/wiki/Phrygia" title="Phrygia">
       Phrygia
      </a>
      ) were forced to pay tribute. His
      <i>
       stele
      </i>
      has been found as far west as
      <a href="/wiki/Larnaca" title="Larnaca">
       Larnaca
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">
       Cyprus
      </a>
      . Sargon II conquered
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Gurgum&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Gurgum (page does not exist)">
       Gurgum
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Milid" title="Milid">
       Milid
      </a>
      , the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Georgian_people" title="Georgian people">
       Georgian
      </a>
      state of
      <a href="/wiki/Tabal" title="Tabal">
       Tabal
      </a>
      , and all of the Neo-
      <a href="/wiki/Hittites" title="Hittites">
       Hittite
      </a>
      kingdoms of the
      <a href="/wiki/Taurus_Mountains" title="Taurus Mountains">
       Taurus Mountains
      </a>
      .
      <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">
       Egypt
      </a>
      , now under a new
      <a href="/wiki/Nubia" title="Nubia">
       Nubian
      </a>
      dynasty, once again attempted to gain ground in the region by supporting
      <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Israel_(Samaria)" title="Kingdom of Israel (Samaria)">
       Israel's
      </a>
      rebellion against the empire, however Sargon II once again crushed the uprising, and
      <a href="/wiki/Piye" title="Piye">
       Piye
      </a>
      was routed and driven back over the
      <a href="/wiki/Sinai_Peninsula" title="Sinai Peninsula">
       Sinai
      </a>
      . Sargon II was killed in 705 BC while on a punitive raid against the
      <a href="/wiki/Cimmerians" title="Cimmerians">
       Cimmerians
      </a>
      , and was succeeded by
      <a href="/wiki/Sennacherib" title="Sennacherib">
       Sennacherib
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Sennacherib" title="Sennacherib">
       Sennacherib
      </a>
      (705-681 BC), a ruthless ruler, defeated the
      <a href="/wiki/Greeks" title="Greeks">
       Greeks
      </a>
      who were attempting to gain a foothold in
      <a href="/wiki/Cilicia" title="Cilicia">
       Cilicia
      </a>
      , and then defeated and drove the
      <a href="/wiki/Nubia" title="Nubia">
       Nubian
      </a>
      ruled
      <a href="/wiki/Egyptians" title="Egyptians">
       Egyptians
      </a>
      from the
      <a href="/wiki/Near_East" title="Near East">
       Near East
      </a>
      where the new Nubian Pharaoh
      <a href="/wiki/Taharqa" title="Taharqa">
       Taharqa
      </a>
      had once again fomented revolt against Assyria among the
      <a href="/wiki/Israelites" title="Israelites">
       Israelites
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Judeans" title="Judeans">
       Judeans
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canaanites" title="Canaanites">
       Canaanites
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Sennacherib" title="Sennacherib">
       Sennacherib
      </a>
      was forced to contend with a major revolt within his empire, which included a large alliance of subject peoples, including
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Babylonians" title="Babylonians">
       Babylonians
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Persian_people" title="Persian people">
       Persians
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Medes" title="Medes">
       Medes
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Chaldea" title="Chaldea">
       Chaldeans
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Elamites" title="Elamites">
       Elamites
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parthians" title="Parthians">
       Parthians
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manneans" title="Manneans">
       Manneans
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Arameans" title="Arameans">
       Arameans
      </a>
      . The prime movers in this rebellion were
      <a href="/wiki/Mushezib-Marduk" title="Mushezib-Marduk">
       Mushezib-Marduk
      </a>
      of Babylonia,
      <a href="/wiki/Achaemenes" title="Achaemenes">
       Achaemenes
      </a>
      of Persia,
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Khumban-umena_III&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Khumban-umena III (page does not exist)">
       Khumban-umena III
      </a>
      of Elam, and
      <a href="/wiki/Deioces" title="Deioces">
       Deioces
      </a>
      of Media. The
      <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Halule" title="Battle of Halule">
       Battle of Halule
      </a>
      was fought in 691 BC between Sennacherib and his enemies, in which this vast alliance failed to overthrow Sennacherib. The Assyrian king was then able to subjugate these nations individually,
      <a href="/wiki/Babylon" title="Babylon">
       Babylon
      </a>
      was sacked and largely destroyed by Sennacherib.
     </p>
     <p>
      He sacked
      <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Israel_(Samaria)" title="Kingdom of Israel (Samaria)">
       Israel
      </a>
      , subjugated the
      <a href="/wiki/Samaritans" title="Samaritans">
       Samaritans
      </a>
      and laid siege to
      <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Judah" title="Kingdom of Judah">
       Judah
      </a>
      , forcing tribute upon it. He installed his own son
      <a href="/wiki/Ashur-nadin-shumi" title="Ashur-nadin-shumi">
       Ashur-nadin-shumi
      </a>
      as king in Babylonia. He maintained Assyrian domination over the Medes, Manneans and Persians to the east, Asia Minor and the southern Caucasus to the north and north west, and the Levant, Phoenicia and Aram in the west.
     </p>
     <p>
      Sennacherib's palace and garden at
      <a href="/wiki/Nineveh" title="Nineveh">
       Nineveh
      </a>
      have been proposed by some scholars as the true location of the
      <a href="/wiki/Hanging_Gardens_of_Babylon" title="Hanging Gardens of Babylon">
       Hanging Gardens of Babylon
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
       <a href="#cite_note-45">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        44
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It was during the reign of Sennacherib that the previously minor city of
      <a href="/wiki/Nineveh" title="Nineveh">
       Nineveh
      </a>
      (extant since approximately 3000 BC) was transformed into the capital of Assyria, growing at its height to be the largest city in the world at the time, with a population of up to 150,000 people.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
       <a href="#cite_note-46">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        45
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Sennacherib was murdered by his own sons (according to the Bible the sons were named
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adrammelech" title="Adrammelech">
       Adrammelech
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Abimelech" title="Abimelech">
       Abimelech
      </a>
      and
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Sharezer&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Sharezer (page does not exist)">
       Sharezer
      </a>
      ) in a palace revolt, apparently in revenge for the destruction of Babylon, a city sacred to all Mesopotamians, including the Assyrians.
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lachishsiege1.PNG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="408" data-file-width="612" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Lachishsiege1.PNG/220px-Lachishsiege1.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Lachishsiege1.PNG/330px-Lachishsiege1.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Lachishsiege1.PNG/440px-Lachishsiege1.PNG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lachishsiege1.PNG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Judea" title="Judea">
         Judean
        </a>
        captives being led away into slavery by the Assyrians after the
        <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Lachish" title="Siege of Lachish">
         siege of Lachish
        </a>
        in 701 BC
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Esarhaddon" title="Esarhaddon">
       Esarhaddon
      </a>
      (680669 BC) expanded Assyria still further, campaigning deep into the
      <a href="/wiki/Caucasus_Mountains" title="Caucasus Mountains">
       Caucasus Mountains
      </a>
      in the north, defeating king
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rusas_II" title="Rusas II">
       Rusas II
      </a>
      and breaking
      <a href="/wiki/Urartu" title="Urartu">
       Urartu
      </a>
      completely in the process. Esarhaddon campaigned successfully subjugating the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scythian" title="Scythian">
       Scythian
      </a>
      king
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ishpakaia" title="Ishpakaia">
       Ishpakaia
      </a>
      , and the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cimmerian" title="Cimmerian">
       Cimmerian
      </a>
      king
      <a href="/wiki/Teushpa" title="Teushpa">
       Teushpa
      </a>
      in Asia Minor, and in Ancient Iran, the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manneans" title="Manneans">
       Manneans
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gutians" title="Gutians">
       Gutians
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Persian_people" title="Persian people">
       Persians
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Phraortes" title="Phraortes">
       Phraortes
      </a>
      the king of the
      <a href="/wiki/Medes" title="Medes">
       Medes
      </a>
      were subjugated.
     </p>
     <p>
      To the west, the kings of
      <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Judah" title="Kingdom of Judah">
       Judah
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Edom" title="Edom">
       Edom
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Moab" title="Moab">
       Moab
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">
       Israel
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Sidon" title="Sidon">
       Sidon
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Ekron" title="Ekron">
       Ekron
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Byblos" title="Byblos">
       Byblos
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arvad" title="Arvad">
       Arvad
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Samarra" title="Samarra">
       Samarra
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Ammon" title="Ammon">
       Ammon
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Amalek" title="Amalek">
       Amalek
      </a>
      , and the ten
      <a href="/wiki/Greeks" title="Greeks">
       Greek
      </a>
      kings of
      <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">
       Cyprus
      </a>
      , are listed as Assyrian subjects.
     </p>
     <p>
      Tiring of
      <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Egypt" title="Ancient Egypt">
       Egyptian
      </a>
      interference in the Assyrian Empire, Esarhaddon decided to conquer Egypt. In 671 BC crossed the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sinai_Desert" title="Sinai Desert">
       Sinai Desert
      </a>
      , and invaded and took
      <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">
       Egypt
      </a>
      with surprising ease and speed, driving its foreign
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nubian_people" title="Nubian people">
       Nubian
      </a>
      /
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kushite" title="Kushite">
       Kushite
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">
       Ethiopian
      </a>
      rulers out and destroying the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kushite_Empire" title="Kushite Empire">
       Kushite Empire
      </a>
      in the process. Esarhaddon now declared himself "king of
      <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">
       Egypt
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">
       Libya
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Kush" title="Kingdom of Kush">
       Kush
      </a>
      ", and returned with rich booty from the cities of the delta; he erected a victory stele at this time, and paraded the captive Nubian Prince
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ushankhuru&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ushankhuru (page does not exist)">
       Ushankhuru
      </a>
      , the son of Taharqa in Nineveh. Esarhaddon stationed a small army in northern Egypt and describes how; "All Ethiopians (read Nubians/Kushites) I deported from Egypt, leaving not one left to do homage to me".[69] He installed native Egyptian princes throughout the land to rule on his behalf.[70] The conquest by Esarhaddon effectively marked the end of the short lived Kushite Empire.
     </p>
     <p>
      He expanded the empire as far south as
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabia" title="Arabia">
       Arabia
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Meluhha" title="Meluhha">
       Meluhha
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Dilmun" title="Dilmun">
       Dilmun
      </a>
      (modern
      <a href="/wiki/Bahrain" title="Bahrain">
       Bahrain
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Qatar" title="Qatar">
       Qatar
      </a>
      ).
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Esarhaddon" title="Esarhaddon">
       Esarhaddon
      </a>
      also completely rebuilt
      <a href="/wiki/Babylon" title="Babylon">
       Babylon
      </a>
      during his reign, bringing peace to Mesopotamia as a whole. The
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Babylonians" title="Babylonians">
       Babylonians
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Egyptians" title="Egyptians">
       Egyptians
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Elamites" title="Elamites">
       Elamites
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Cimmerians" title="Cimmerians">
       Cimmerians
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Scythians" title="Scythians">
       Scythians
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Persia" title="Persia">
       Persians
      </a>
